River and Sea Navigators Must Pass Exams 175

To Prepare for the Dismissal of Foreign Sailors

During the current period of recovering navigation rights, various Chinese shipping companies are actively seeking to expand. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's new Northeast route has already dispatched the Tunam, and the surface rights on the Yangtze River occupied by foreign ships are also being gradually recovered. With time, this goal will be gradually achieved. However, there is a lack of navigation specialists. Most of the Chinese merchant ships hire foreign sailors. This year, a batch of students from the navigation department of the China Merchants School have been sent to ships for practical training. The Zhengji Company has dismissed about 124 senior Japanese sailors, retaining only 81 and gradually replacing them with Chinese personnel. The Central Legislative Yuan has specially formulated the Regulations on Examination of River and Sea Navigators to promote domestic navigators, allowing qualified Chinese to apply and take the examination to ensure that no talent is wasted. Foreign navigators can also be gradually dismissed. Yesterday, the Executive Yuan ordered the shipping bureaus in Shanghai to announce these regulations and notify their subordinates so that they can prepare for the examination. The main points are recorded below:

Instruction: Executive Yuan Instruction No. 27: Approved the Legislative Yuan's communication stating that the Regulations on Examination of River and Sea Navigators have been formulated, promulgated, and implemented by this Yuan. In addition to distributing them to the administrative organs of the provinces and cities directly under the jurisdiction, they should be announced and the shipping companies should be ordered to notify their subordinate navigators to apply for the examination in accordance with the regulations. (Omitted below) Yesterday, the shipping bureaus in Shanghai received this order and distributed it to their navigators for reference and preparation for the examination in accordance with these regulations.

Regulations: A total of twelve articles. The main points are extracted below: (1) The Regulations on Examination of River and Sea Navigators shall be implemented on the date of promulgation; (2) Those who have not passed the examination shall not be Chinese River and Sea Navigators; (3) The provisions of the preceding article shall apply to all official and commercial ships other than naval warships officers; (3) Any Chinese person with two years or more of river and sea navigation experience and sound physical and eyesight may take the examination; (4) River and Sea Navigators are divided into five grades: special grade captain, captain, first mate, second mate, and third mate; (5) The examination subjects are divided into three categories according to their business: foreign ocean-going, domestic coastal, and river; (6) The examination is divided into oral and written tests, and the subjects include magnetism, hydrostatics, statics, principles of navigation instruments, logarithmic plane, trigonometry, driving method, Ziqian line, International Navigation Collision Regulations, Maritime Law, McQuyck driving, nautical charts, measuring water depth, International flag signals, solar and lunar star altitude, marine rescue, lifeboat work cabin machine overview, and many other items that can be listed. Yesterday, the shipping bureaus distributed them to the navigators of each ship to prepare for the examination in accordance with these regulations.

A Bullet Suddenly Flies Into a Public Bus 176

Breaking Two Panes of Glass

Discussion on Dong Dingsan's House Tax Standard 177

Municipal expert Dong Xiujia previously served as a consultant to the Shanghai Special Municipal Government, Secretary-General of the Hankou Municipal Government, and Director of the Public Works Bureau and Director of the Engineering Bureau. He is currently a member of the Shanghai Municipal Construction Discussion Committee and has a great understanding of Chinese and foreign municipal administration research. A reporter from the National News Agency interviewed Mr. Dong on the matter of the Municipal Council's valuation and collection of house tax and asked for his opinion. According to Mr. Dong, house tax is an important municipal tax in British cities. When collecting house tax in British cities, the standard for taxation is generally based on the actual rental price of the houses. The municipal governments of various cities never arbitrarily estimate the rental price of houses and force citizens to pay taxes according to the price. Now, the Shanghai Municipal Council suspects that the actual rental prices of houses are inaccurate and incomplete and plans to estimate them itself and use its estimated rental price as the standard for collecting total taxes. Citizens are afraid that the Council's appraisers will deliberately overestimate the rent, so the amount of total tax paid in the future will exceed the actual rent. The two sides hold different opinions and have not yet resolved the issue. In fact, the collection of house tax (ie, total tax) has precedents in British cities and has also been adopted as an important municipal tax in Chinese cities for a long time. Generally, it is based on the actual rent, and there is no need for a separate estimate. This can eliminate all the expenses of the appraisers and prevent them from cheating when estimating the rent. In my opinion, the Municipal Council can adopt the following methods to solve this problem: (1) The house tax (ie, total tax) should still be based on the rent reported by the landlords. However, the rent on the property tax bill must be clearly indicated as the basis for the rent. (2) Investigate whether the rent on the property tax bills of each household is accurate. If any false reporting of rent is found, the tax should be collected based on the actual rent, so that the total tax revenue will not be reduced. (3) For self-occupied properties, an estimate must be added, but the rent of nearby properties should be used as a reference during the estimate and should be appropriately reduced, because self-occupied properties are not for profit, so less house tax should be collected to show the Municipal Council's intention to encourage self-owned housing.

"Humanities Monthly" Volume 2, Issue 2 Published 182

With the aim of publishing modern historical materials and providing reference for scholars, the "Humanities Monthly" Volume 2, Issue 2, which specially compiles an index of recent magazine highlights, has been published on schedule. In terms of text, this issue includes Huang Yanpei's "A Study of the Tomb Inscriptions of Tang Chun and His Son Excavated in the Shanghai French Concession, Five Hundred Years Ago," which provides much textual research on the historical geography of Shanghai; Pan Guangdan's "On the Harmony of the Historical View of Humanity and the Rule of Man and the Rule of Law," which analyzes the causes of talent production in detail based on facts, making people pay attention to the importance of maintaining talent and its

perspectives; Wen Yu's "On Opium in the History of China's Foreign Trade," which describes in detail the widespread prevalence of its harm year by year and the increasing outflow of money, allowing readers to gain insight into the daily crisis of the national economy; and Gulu's translation of "A Brief Account of the Circulation of Neo-Confucian Commentaries in Japan," which details the eastward flow of our country's culture and the research of our country's academic situation by Japanese people in previous generations, providing valuable reference for those studying the history of Sino-Japanese culture. As for Jiangdong Adou's "Notes from the Ancient Red Embroidery Pavilion," Xiyin's "Notes from the Xiyin Hall," Yishi's "Also Good Cottage Notes," and Wu Zonglian's "Autobiography," they mostly record eyewitness accounts and personal experiences, which are valuable materials for future historians to refer to. Shen Yougan's "Statistics of Psychological Talents in Various Countries" is a reliable work that introduces specialized books by experts. The index of magazines in this issue contains a total of ninety types, two hundred and eighty-eight volumes, and one thousand nine hundred and ninety-eight new entries. Among the important new publications, the "Historical Materials Bi-Weekly" published by the Palace Museum in Beijing is an important reference for historical researchers. Distribution: Humanities Editorial Office, Nan Qianjiatang, West End, Lafayette Road, Albert Road, Shanghai French Concession. Agents for subscription: Life Weekly Society Newspaper Agency, Shanghai Civilization Bookstore, New Moon Bookstore, and various commercial printing houses in various ports.

Setting Up an Altar for Sutra Chanting and Buddhist Worship at the June 3rd Garden 186

Japan has been using the new calendar for decades, but farmers in the countryside still follow the old customs for farming. The birthday of Sakyamuni Buddha was originally on the eighth day of the fourth lunar month in the old calendar. Now, in order to follow the trend, it has also been changed to the national calendar. The Japanese Buddhist Association in Shanghai has decided to advance the event to April 5th (Sunday) in the new calendar and set up a temporary Buddhist altar at the June 3rd Garden to collectively chant sutras and worship the Buddha. Admission tickets have been distributed to invite Buddhist men and women to participate. Those who have not obtained this ticket only need to purchase artificial flowers at the entrance and hang them on their chests to enter. Each ticket costs a small amount of two dimes, just to cover the expenses. At that time, several cherry blossom trees in the garden will be in full bloom, adding to the visual enjoyment with the help of the Buddha's power. It will definitely be a lively event.

Letter to the Editor 194

Respected Editor of the Great Newspaper: I am writing to inform you that the news column of your newspaper today contains a report stating that all twenty-odd silk factories in Northern Shanghai have gone on strike to demand the restoration of the original fixed wages. This is completely inconsistent with the facts. On the afternoon of March 31, a female worker at the Qingfeng Silk Factory had a quarrel with an employee, which almost led to an incident. The dispute was quickly resolved, and work resumed as usual the next morning. This involved only one person and one factory and did not involve outsiders. The labor unrest that occurred yesterday afternoon was a completely separate matter. No demands were made beforehand, and no one came forward to take responsibility afterward. Although the female workers were blindly following, they all resented the instigators. At that time, Zhou, the director of the Fourth District Bureau of Public Safety, and Wu, the director of the Second Branch of the Fourth District Bureau, personally went to the scene to mediate and separately advise the female workers and inquire about the reasons for the strike. They were all unable to answer. Then, Shen Huaichen, the chairman of our association, and Huang Jinfan, a standing committee member, separately convened representatives of the female workers, including Wu Suzhen, to inquire about the situation in detail. They also claimed that no one had mentioned it beforehand and did not ask for any demands afterward. Although the Women Workers' Association tried its best to investigate, it was all passive. Until after 10:00 PM, the truth could not be ascertained. Therefore, the female workers were advised to return to work as usual tomorrow (i.e., today). As a result, more than a dozen factories have already resumed work this morning. However, timid female workers did not dare to go to the factory, and it was learned that several people were inciting the strike. The police officers have arrested them (the following is omitted). I hereby request that you write a reply. Shanghai Silk Industry Guild Committee.

The China Seafarers' Industrial Federation yesterday issued a document to its branches stating: For order.

Regarding the matter, our association's secretary, Liu Yuzhou, reported that he had read an article in the Shen Bao on the 27th of this month entitled "Shanghai Shipping Companies Discuss Teahouse Attendant Issues." The article stated that Jardine Matheson & Co. said, "The labor union does not allow teahouse attendants to be directly employed by the company," and the shipping association said, "The teahouse attendant system of the seafarers' union is not good, and the seafarers' union is using its union power to encroach on the sovereignty of public affairs." Both of these matters are false and concerning the labor dispute with the teahouse attendants, the main reason is that the company side and the comprador level collect security deposits and other malpractices and do not pay wages. This is the poor system and exercise of sovereignty of the capitalist side, which has been exposed by our association in official documents and publications. Shipping companies do not self-reflect but blame the workers. For the present plan, our association should publish corrections on the one hand, and send letters to question the capitalists on the other hand, and order the Shanghai, Ningbo, Hankou, Jiujiang, and Wenzhou branches to investigate and report on the treatment of teahouse attendants to our association for submission to the central government for verification, so as to avoid confusion and damage to the reputation of our association. The contents of the newspaper and the report form were filed with the court. In accordance with the decision of the 23rd Standing Committee meeting of our association, the report form and the survey form are hereby sent to the association and forwarded to you for immediate compliance with the order to send personnel to investigate the treatment of the workers in the middle class on the ship and fill in the form for submission. The matter concerns the capitalist's slander of the sailors' suffering and the credibility of the union's branches at all levels, so do not neglect it.

Sir/Madam, I recently saw a news item in the newspapers of April 2 concerning the meeting of the municipal industry tax regulations association. The two items discussed concerned the municipal business tax. It was generally stated in the report that the tax rate had been submitted to the Ministry of Finance for review and that the consent of the Chamber of Commerce representatives had not been obtained beforehand and should be denied and rejected for investigation. The draft municipal business tax rate was discussed at a temporary office meeting convened by former Director Tang on March 26, during which the advisors, specialized committee members, and preparation members of the office were convened for a discussion. The attendees expressed their opinions and made slight changes in preparation for another scheduled meeting to invite representatives of the Chamber of Commerce to participate in the opinions and make revisions before submitting them to the Municipal Government for consultation with the Ministry of Finance. This was stated publicly by the chairman at the meeting at that time. Later, because former Director Tang resigned due to illness, there was a scheduled handover that was not completed. Now that the newly appointed Director Cai has taken over, a meeting will be scheduled to notify the representatives of the Chamber of Commerce to discuss matters. The investigation and filing of reports are separate matters that have not yet been implemented. The fact that the previously reported tax rate has been sent to the ministry is not true and is a rumor that should be corrected to avoid misunderstandings. In addition to sending a letter to the Chamber of Commerce, I hope that you will investigate and make corrections quickly. This letter is addressed to the Editorial Department of the Shen Bao and the Preparatory Office of the Business Tax of the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau. April 2.

Free Talk

World Anecdotes 195

— Hai Ke

▲ Several prehistoric animal bones have been dredged up from the North Sea in Europe, leading to the belief that the North Sea was a dry land millions of years ago.

▲ American automobile magnate Henry Ford once said to people, "Don't start saving before you're forty." He also said that he had never thought of making a fortune in his life, yet he became rich.

▲ A woman in South London was fined for confining her dog in a room for seven years without letting it out for exercise. The woman argued that it was not her intention not to let it out, but because it suffered from rheumatism.

▲ A large amount of substandard oak wood is imported into Europe. The wood has countless small holes bored by weevils, but people who counterfeit antique wooden objects welcome them very much, and the market is excellent.

▲ Ten years ago, a kind of red squirrel was native to England and could often be seen in London. In recent years, American gray squirrels have been imported into England. For some reason, the red squirrels have been disappearing day by day.

▲ An airplane in Newcastle, England, was taking off when it was suddenly attacked by a cow, causing a lot of damage and preventing it from flying away. The cow was not injured.

Japanese Female Teacher Commits Suicide Under Train Wheels 196

— Chen Yuanliang

The cause of suicide is nothing more than weakness of will or temporary indignation. However, the methods of death are different. Some use medicine to reduce the physical pain, while others use drastic methods that make people exclaim in horror. The recent tragic suicide of a female teacher in Nishikyo, Japan, is one example. According to reports, there is a girls' school in the area. Ms. Nakkamura, a teacher at the school, is young, well-educated, and graceful with a silver tongue. However, she was born at the wrong time. Her parents passed away, leaving behind two sisters who were both of school age. She relied solely on her older sister. Ms. Nakkamura had an open mind and could not bear to see them lose their opportunity to study. However, her career as a teacher was also quite difficult. Where could she find extra money to subsidize her sisters' education? A certain coffee shop was recruiting waitresses. Ms. Nakkamura heard the news and resolutely applied. From then on, after finishing her classes, she would apply makeup and put on silks and brocades again before rushing to the shop to spend her life serving customers. She would not return home until two o'clock the next morning, which was also said to be difficult. At that time, there were many coffee shops in the city, and they competed fiercely for business, showing off their strange and ingenious ways of attracting customers. They recruited waitresses to attract customers, but most of the employees were mediocre, and few were as beautiful and intelligent as Ms. Nakkamura. Customers who talked to her found her talk eloquent and were happy and forgot their fatigue. As a result, they all flocked to the shop, and the shop's business flourished. At that time, a certain journalist secretly learned the inside story and quickly drafted an article and submitted it to a major newspaper. The next morning, the newspaper was published and spread throughout the city. The matter was heard by the person in charge of the school, who thought it was related to the school's reputation and immediately summoned her to show her the news. Ms. Nakkamura admitted it directly and stated that she would rather sacrifice her appearance than sit idly by and watch her sisters lose their opportunity to study. The person in charge of the school said that the school was a place for chanting and learning and bore the responsibility of enlightening culture. How could it tolerate this mixing of the tracks, a place of drunken gold and paper fans, and harm young people? He decided to dismiss her. Ms. Nakkamura's heart was broken by this blow. The next day, she went out and lay down on the railroad tracks. Suddenly, a fast train sped straight down. By the time the people on the train noticed, her limbs were separated, and her flesh and blood were blurred. The loss of such a beauty is truly shocking and heartbreaking.

A Record of the Patriotic Girls' School Welcoming New School Directors 197

— Yu Jianhua

The Patriotic Girls' School was founded thirty years ago and is the oldest. Since moving to the new school building on Jiangwan Road last year, it has been actively expanding and striving to improve. It is currently adding a sheltered playground, offices, classrooms, and dormitories, and is building mountains with stones and ponds on the campus, with prosperous flowers and trees and abundant peach and plum trees. The future development is immeasurable. Recently, Mr. Chu Minyi was invited to be a school director. A welcome meeting was held at the school at 3:00 PM on the 28th of last month, and Mr. Chu was invited to give a speech. The speech was very long and cannot be fully recorded. I will extract some of the interesting points to fill this talk.

▲ Listening to Lectures and Going Home: The day was a Saturday, and there were no classes after noon. Students were either going home, visiting friends, or shopping, and their luggage was ready. The school issued a temporary curfew, and no one was allowed to leave the school except for special circumstances. So, there was no choice but to listen to the lectures at school.

▲ Tang Monk and Lama: Mr. Chu arrived at 3:30 PM, full of energy. He first wore a black hat that was flat in the middle. Some said he looked like Tang Monk, and others said he looked like a Tibetan Lama.

▲ Roses and Weeds: Mr. Chu said that although China has four hundred million people, too many are illiterate. The reason is that girls' schools are not developed, and children have no opportunity to learn to read in the home. The quality of a person is half due to innate factors and half due to acquired factors. He took the roses made of paper that were placed on the table as a metaphor. Those who are good innately are like good seeds, and those who are good acquired are like fertile planting ground. Only when both are good can there be beautiful flowers. If parents are ignorant and uneducated, it is already a bad seed. If children are born and not educated, they will become a bunch of weeds. How can China not be in a mess if three hundred million of the four hundred million compatriots are weeds?

▲ Father's Fault and Mother's Fault: Educating children is the duty of citizens. Excellent children should be educated by their parents personally and should not be entrusted to nurses. If they have no power to raise or teach, it is best not to have children. The Three Character Classic says, "It is the father's fault not to educate." Now we can add a sentence: "It is the mother's fault not to raise."

▲ Chopsticks and Hand Washing: If you want excellent children, you must pay attention to family education and cultivate good habits. You must pay attention to and correct children's every move. Otherwise, habits will be difficult to change for life. For example, if you don't pay attention to holding chopsticks when you are young, you may not be able to do it properly even after you grow up. The use of chopsticks in China can be said to be the most convenient. By using them, you don't have to wash your hands when you eat because your hands do not come into direct contact with the food (note: this is true for eating rice in the south, but not for eating steamed buns in the north, which requires direct use of hands). Westerners originally used their hands, but then they used forks, and eating bread requires direct use of hands, so they must develop the habit of washing their hands before meals.

▲ Good Morning and Good Night: Etiquette is also very important. Whether classmates or teachers, they must greet each other when they meet. Westerners say good morning and good night at home, which is learned from childhood and has a great relationship with emotions.

▲ Royal Way and Hegemonic Way: The sports in schools now are mostly imported, such as track and field, soccer, and basketball, which are either too intense or too expensive, and require a large number of people and a large venue. They are not possible for everyone. National skills are gentle, frugal, and can be practiced by anyone, with few drawbacks. Western methods are mostly hegemonic, while national skills are mostly royal.

▲ Exercise and Definition: The definition of movement is to unblock the blood, and the definition of exercise is to move the muscles and bones.

▲ Tai Chi Quan and Tai Chi Exercises: Tai Chi Quan is an internal skill for boxers and is very beneficial to people's health, but it is too complicated, and most people are not patient enough to learn it. Therefore, we take its meaning to create Tai Chi exercises, which are simple and clear and can be explained with books. The movements are not complicated and easy to remember, and both old and young can practice them.

▲ Students and Teachers: After the lecture, we went to the playground together. First, the physical education students performed national skills, and then Mr. Chu performed Tai Chi exercises and Tai Chi Quan. After the performance, Mr. Chu nodded and smiled amid applause.

Ways of Loving 198

— Miao Zi

In old Chinese novels, the men depicted in love stories are like Jia Baoyu, and the women are like Lin Daiyu. Or the men are like Fang Qing, and the women are like Chen Cuie. In short, the men must be effeminate to win the women's affection, and the women must naturally be frail to be even more endearing.

However, the men who are infatuated with Western beauties are like those in the novels of Hall Caine, such as the knight, Greeg, who are heroic, valiant and show the unique greatness of men. From the Middle Ages until now, although those knights in crested helmets and with swords have become historical figures, their influence has not faded away. Ordinary sports stars and even striving warriors still retain their supreme glory and often provide passionate fuel for humorous love stories.

Looking at it from the perspective of films, in the West, whether it's Valentino, Colman, Ramon Novarro, Charles Farrell, or Charles Rogers, in 90% of the love films, the male protagonist is a hero, or they all believe that this is the way to express the "life force of love."

In China, however, it is not the same. Although the style of Chinese films is different, I have seen that the male protagonists in many love films are often a rich young master or a writer or artist. Therefore, some people say that the Chinese Carmen would never fall in love with a bullfighting strongman, and this statement seems quite believable.

However, the wheel of time is rolling toward the peak of strength. That kind of weak love depiction has obviously lost its life stimulus. From the perspective of films, some chaotic and unbearable martial arts films, although also very stimulating, have unfortunately lost the spirit of the times. What we expect now is that kind of spiritual and powerful impact that jumps out of the circle of affectation and artificiality—the impact of love and strength.

Here, I cannot help but like the success of the recent domestic film "Three Arrows of Love," which was produced by the Star Film Company. Although it does not have a modern setting, it is rich in a spirit that surpasses modernity, and the male and female protagonists in the film are all typical heroes in our ideal. This is bound to give us new stimuli after we watch the way of love depicted in this new film.

Overseas Personalities 199

— Yuan Yuan

▲Gandhi's Triumphant Song: Without fists or courage, unadorned and barefoot (Gandhi, bare-chested, only draped in a homespun cloth), a dwarfed and hunched old man of a subjugated nation actually defeated the world's first-class British Empire with its naval, land, and air forces. This is an unprecedented spectacle in the history of all mankind. Since Mahatma Gandhi, the leader of the Indian National Congress and a sage, announced a policy of passive resistance against the British government last year, he has been imprisoned again, causing shock at home and abroad. The British government specially convened the London Round Table Conference, allowing Indian delegates to attend to discuss federal autonomy. Participants included hundreds of representatives from various Indian princes, sectors, and levels. However, the final resolution still required the approval of this uncrowned king, the highest authority who had just emerged from prison. Gandhi, from being a prisoner, suddenly became a guest of honor, engaging in equal talks with the British Empire's representative, the Governor-General of India. On February 4th of this year, the two sides signed a treaty. The British Empire recognized the abandonment of its right to rule over India's internal affairs and abolished centuries-old traditional policies such as the salt monopoly. Most party members were returned their confiscated property, and freedom of speech, publication, assembly, and all political criticism were restored. The right to peacefully boycott British goods was recognized as a legitimate act. Thus, Gandhi declared a temporary cessation of the non-cooperation movement but continued to demand complete independence from Britain and petitioned the native princes to open up their political power and implement democracy. This was Gandhi's first great triumph in his life and a major symbol of the resurgence of Eastern national culture. According to reports, on the day of the signing of the treaty, Gandhi rose before dawn and led his disciples in raising their hands to the sky in prayer as usual, remaining silent for half an hour. As the morning light dawned, suddenly a loud roar resounded like the collapse of the sky and the stampede of ten thousand horses. Tens of thousands of adoring elderly, young, men, and women outside the group eagerly cheered, vying to catch a glimpse of his moral character and listen to his legal pronouncements. Gandhi is truly a remarkable and outstanding figure!

▲Einstein's Farewell Dinner: Since the great German scientist Einstein came to America last winter, he has been deeply researching the principles of the universe and revising and re-publishing the theory of relativity. On the other hand, he has also been wandering in the mountains and rivers, indulging in literature and wine, spending about a hundred days living and playing on the Pacific coast. Now, on March 4th, he is taking advantage of a German ship to return to his country from New York. Various circles and groups held a grand farewell ceremony as if for a king. Einstein himself said, "No one dares to accept such kindness." This is not just a humble remark. Einstein, being Jewish, the New York tycoons, three-tenths of whom belong to the Jewish community, specially initiated a farewell banquet before his departure, with each person's seat fee being one hundred US dollars. After deducting expenses, all the proceeds were donated to the new Jewish colony in Palestine. That evening, more than a thousand people attended, raising 100,000 US dollars in cash in one fell swoop. Einstein gave a speech using a radio broadcast, praising the achievements of the Palestinian colony over the past ten years, and said that the conflict between Jews and Arabs should be resolved through joint negotiation by the two ethnic groups and should not rely solely on the British government's guarantees and mediation. His words indirectly expressed dissatisfaction with Britain's current policy towards Palestine. It is recalled that when Einstein first arrived and gave speeches advocating peace movements and urging citizens to reject military service, he was fiercely opposed by the American warlords, leading to proposals to deport him. Einstein is indeed rich in human sympathy and is not only a cold-headed astronomical expert. Very few people can understand the theories he has published, and when asked why, Einstein smiled and said, "I am not a psychologist and am ashamed that I cannot provide an answer for others."

▲Mussolini's Demonstration: Italian Prime Minister, Fascist Party dictator Mussolini, with his fierce and decisive style, is unparalleled for a time. Although his personality differs from that of the Soviet Union's Stalin, who is deep, formidable and ruthless, their capabilities are evenly matched, and their spheres of influence are almost evenly divided in the world. Last month, an American admiral gave a speech at a tea party in Philadelphia, saying that Mussolini had once run over a girl with his own car. A wealthy American in the car asked to stop to check on her, but Mussolini laughed and said, "When we deal with the world, we only move forward and do not look back. Moreover, what is the life of one person worth?" When this statement was spread, the Italian ambassador to the United States received a telegram from Mussolini instructing him to demand concrete evidence from the US government. The US Secretary of State was immediately alarmed and at a loss and telegraphed an apology to Mussolini and ordered a military court to try the admiral for making the remarks. The American public was in an uproar, and members of Congress also raised questions, ridiculing it as a humiliation to the nation. The US Secretary of State, based on the admiral's self-defense, stated that it was hearsay and only said at a tea party, not daring to openly insult an important figure from a friendly country. The military trial was changed to a reprimand, but a formal apology was made to Italy. Mussolini was also complacent. Afterwards, the US Assistant Attorney General made a speech, saying, "Recently, the cost of living has been increasing, and the official salary is not enough to cover expenses. Fortunately, I was not born in Italy, otherwise, one word from the Prime Minister would not only not increase my salary but also reduce it, and my family's livelihood would be even more difficult." Mussolini again telegraphed the Italian ambassador to interrogate the Assistant Attorney General, who then published an explanation in the newspaper the next day, expressing that there was no criticism. Mussolini then chose not to pursue the matter. It is said that one sees the rabbit in three days, and it transforms into a lion or an elephant. It is also said that a fierce tiger in the mountains does not gather wild herbs. Mussolini's external arrogance is so strange!

Grains: Ke Xian and Ke Hua Stagnant

Newly Arrived Foreign Rice Directly Transshipped

Yesterday, the Ke Xian market was sluggish because local merchants had not inquired for many days, and the market appeared even more stagnant. The Jiangxi rice purchased by Pu Hu a few days ago was being offered for sale at a discounted price because there was no further development in the market, but the local market had no intention of inquiring, and the Ke Bang had no appetite. Although they wanted to sell, there was no buyer, so the market price continued to fall. Yesterday, the local market responded to Jiangxi Ji with 300 packages at a price of only 10 yuan and 6 jiao and 4 fen to 06 jiao. The price was also slightly lower than the price sold the day before yesterday, with a difference of only a few jiao and more than 2 jiao. Furthermore, two small batches of foreign rice transported by Japanese merchants the day before yesterday and yesterday were directly shipped to various provinces in the north and south and along the Yangtze River because they were difficult to sell in Shanghai, so they have not yet been sold in the Shanghai market.

The Flour Market Fluctuates Greatly 207

Soaring in the Morning...Plunging in the Afternoon

The Closing Still Looks Good...Turnover of 1.8 Million

Yesterday, the flour market saw huge ups and downs in the morning and afternoon sessions, showing the full extent of the competition between the two sides. When the market first opened in the morning, foreign wheat was quoted at a small increase of two or three jiao, and outside long positions were still hidden. By the second session, the situation had become urgent. It was rumored that the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, in view of the smooth sales of factories, believed that foreign wheat had a great impact on Chinese farmers. With the new wheat about to enter the market, if continuous ordering was allowed, it would not be a good sign. Therefore, those who ordered in the future had to register in advance or be subject to prohibition. Once this was spread, the hearts of people inside and outside the industry (a small factory also rushed to replenish more than 100,000) suddenly became tense, and those who rushed to buy were extremely enthusiastic. The market also rose sharply, nearly four fen higher for near-term contracts and five or six fen higher for far-term contracts compared to the opening. However, when the market opened in the afternoon, people's hearts changed suddenly. The prohibition was not yet timely. The far-term contracts were related to a part of the market, and the near-term chips had been determined, so it was still necessary to see how the actual sales were. Therefore, floating shorts became very active again, and factories such as Fufeng and Xinda took the opportunity to sell in large quantities, causing the market to plunge again. The total transaction volume for the day reached more than 1.8 million, which shows how lively it was at the time. However, the closing result still looked good, with April up 2.5 fen, May up 2 fen, June and July up 1.75 fen, August up 1.5 fen, and September up 2.25 fen.

Speculation Heat in the Wheat Futures Market 208

Several Ups and Downs...The Result Still Rose

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat futures market in the morning, the market for each month was stable because foreign wheat was quoted at a small increase of two or three jiao, and although people's hearts were good, they were still calm. Compared with the previous day's closing price, there was a difference of one or two fen. However, when the market opened in the afternoon, people's hearts became very tense. Taking advantage of the sharp rise in the flour market in the morning, those who went long and those who were eager to close out short positions flocked in, making the market extremely enthusiastic. Therefore, the highest opening price for this month was 3 taels 8 qian 9 fen, 3 taels 9 qian 2 fen for April, 3 taels 9 qian for June and July, 3 taels 9 qian 3 fen for August, and 3 taels 9 qian and a half for September. The excitement of the market can be imagined. Unexpectedly, the opening price of the second session was like fleeting clouds, leaving no trace. As the flour market had slightly turned down, the short positions of large traders also sold out, so the prices for each month immediately plummeted. The difference between the highest and lowest prices in the two sessions was as much as one qian, and as little as seven or eight fen. The intensity of speculative heat was rarely seen in recent times. Afterwards, each session generally revolved without any breakthrough. As a result, this month was up 4 fen compared to the previous day, May was up 5 fen, June was up 4 fen, July was up 3 fen, August was up 4 fen, and September was up in fen.

Sugar Market: Raw Sugar and White Sugar Steadily Rise

Japanese Sugar Initially Rises, Then Weakens

Yesterday, the sugar market received a telegram from the producing area that the current price of Cuban raw sugar had rebounded by 1.5625 compared to the previous telegram. The prices of New York sugar futures for each month remained unchanged. The new price for March of the next year was 1.64. The current price of Javanese raw sugar remained unchanged. The buying price for April futures was down 1.25, May was down 2.5, and the new price for June was 8.125. The market in the association was even stronger because the foreign exchange rate suddenly rose and demand was slightly higher. The price of Dutch sugar No. 24 raw white sugar was 10 taels and 3 qian, with more than a thousand bags traded. The trend was still stable. Transactions of Japanese sugar were also still active, but there were quite a few shipments, and the market later declined. Z Mark 10 taels 1 qian and 5 fen, YT Mark 10 taels 1 qian 1 fen and 2 li and a half to 10 taels 1 qian, YRO Mark 9 taels 7 qian to 6 qian and a half, YP Mark initially 10 taels 3 qian and a half, but later also fell to 10 taels 3 qian, J Mark 10 taels 4 qian. The market gradually became stable.

Wufu White Ice Will Arrive Today 209

Recently, due to the small amount of Wufu White Ice arriving and the Xiamen factory being out of production, there is not much stock in Shanghai. The stock had already run out the day before yesterday. After the agent telegraphed to urge shipment, it was reported yesterday that a batch had been shipped from the factory and would arrive in Shanghai soon to meet the sales needs of various gangs. If necessary, the factory will be restarted to avoid stockouts.

Silk, Tea, Sichuan and Han Cloth Prices Remain Firm

Recently, due to political disputes in Sichuan Province, the source of yellow and white silk head has been interrupted, and the French merchants' ventures have not changed. The stock in Shanghai is scarce, and the market is becoming stronger. Yesterday, Bailly Anqi and others imported 180 dan of Sichuan and Han cloth, with a price of 47 taels.

Shanghai Factory Completely Shut Down 210

Yesterday, the foreign silk market in this port became even more silent because the overseas silk market did not rise. The telegraph price was slightly lower, and a labor strike broke out in a part of the silk factory in Zhabei. The factory owners were discouraged and the market was stagnant. Yesterday, only Xinfu imported 10 packages of white Da Jing silk, and Kechang and others imported 13 packages of yellow crude silk. The price was still flat and weak.
